  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b78f06b7-53f6-467b-aed3-cbdd8880f8d0'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText16482218339077220079" style="display:none">Miss Kate Daltry doesn't believe in fairy tales . . . or happily ever after.<br /><br />Forced by her stepmother to attend a ball, Kate meets a prince... and decides he's anything but charming. A clash of wits and wills ensues, but they both know their irresistible attraction will lead nowhere. For Gabriel is promised to another woman—a princess whose hand in marriage will fulfill his ruthless ambitions.<br /><br />Gabriel <i>likes</i> his fiancee, which is a welcome turn of events, but he doesn't <i>love</i> her. Obviously, he should be <i>wooing</i> his bride-to-be, not the witty, impoverished beauty who refuses to fawn over him. <br /><br />Godmothers and glass slippers notwithstanding, this is one fairy tale in which destiny conspires to destroy any chance that Kate and Gabriel might have a happily ever after.<br /><br />Unless a prince throws away everything that makes him noble... <br /><br />Unless a dowry of an unruly heart trumps a fortune... <br /><br />Unless one kiss at the stroke of midnight changes everything.</span>

<a href="/questions/605704-does-this-characters-in-the-book-was">Does this characters in the book was mentioned in the other books in the series ? I wanted to read Once upon the tower first </a>
</div>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/36593980-eleanor-shakespeare"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1415110181i/36593980._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/36593980-eleanor-shakespeare">Eleanor Shakespeare</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">No. The series just has the land it's set in, in common. Each story has it's own heroine and hero in it so you can start at any book you like :) They <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">No. The series just has the land it's set in, in common. Each story has it's own heroine and hero in it so you can start at any book you like :) They might be good for stand alones because it is different heroines and heros (but I can't say because I've only read this one so far). Hope this helps and have a good Christmas<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_117565448" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/117565448" />
    <a title="Rane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1987431-rane"><img alt="Rane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419878997p2/1987431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117565448?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rane" href="/user/show/1987431-rane">Rane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=regency-napoleonic-era">regency-napoleonic-era</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117565448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4991418901374088718"><i><b>Once upon a time..not to long ago.</b> A reviewer named Rane came across a book, but not just any book- a book with a beautiful cover in shades of the fairy tale Cinderella. Now Rane has read many good things about this book, and the stars bestowed upon showed it’s favor to other readers. So taking a chance, she picked up this book and took it home with her, hoping all turned out well, if not she could complain loudly.<br/> <br/> Thankfully, Rane did not have to complain and saved her vocal cords the trauma. </i></span>
  <span id="freeText4991418901374088718" style="display:none"><i><b>Once upon a time..not to long ago.</b> A reviewer named Rane came across a book, but not just any book- a book with a beautiful cover in shades of the fairy tale Cinderella. Now Rane has read many good things about this book, and the stars bestowed upon showed it’s favor to other readers. So taking a chance, she picked up this book and took it home with her, hoping all turned out well, if not she could complain loudly.<br /> <br /> Thankfully, Rane did not have to complain and saved her vocal cords the trauma. Now Rane had to admit, she’s never been fond of this author’s works, but was willing to give everyone their chance, was happily surprised at the delightful story. With a lead named Kate was not as meek or weak or a songbird of Cinderellas of old, no this heroine was strong and cunning. As Rane read on, about Kate who was forced to take the role of her sister, the story moved on very quickly, as Kate is forced through one obstacle or another. Having to keep her disguise, Kate the heroine meets up with her- unknownn to her- own godmother, that doesn’t wave around a wand with magic, but is feisty and could talk anyone down man, woman or beast. And whom Rane had to admit was her favorite character throughout the book. We finally meet the prince whom was not Prince Charming, but could be very conceited, but caring to his family and others, his love for history made him smart, but it was up to the strong Kate to turn him on his head and his ways. <br /> <br /> Now Rane did enjoy the story and the leads very much, (and could admit had a crush on the prince’s brother Wick) sadly the Prince Gabriel in all his fine feathers was lacking in her eyes. Rane couldn’t place her finger on what was lacking until she saw she was in the middle of the book by then, when it dawned on her, the lack of growth and stage present the Prince Gabriel had. The time focus on Kate was all and well, but this took away from Kate and Prince Gabriel, and this just wouldn’t do for Rane the Reviewer. As the story progress, with rats that were really cute dogs, and truths finally known and of course glass slippers! Rane was happy with all the nice twists the story had to offer on an classic fairy tale. Even with some nice love scenes- save Rane’s blushes!<br /><br /> As Rane reached the end of this book, she proclaimed to all “This was a fun and delightful book indeed!” and that was all. <br /> As she wrote of this funny little review for all those to read, she sighed happy waiting for the next in the series as she went onto her next book journey<br /><br /> <s>The End</s>.....Until the next Review!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4991418901374088718" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1818932633361469194">A Cinderella re-telling in Historical Romance? Count me in!<br/><br/>Except, well, Cinderella was always too much of a victim for me. So, when I met the heroine of this book, Kate, color me surprised. She fought with the evil stepmother constantly, and the only reason she would give in to the stepmother's demands was to protect the servants and tenant farmers. So, I liked her. Not doormatty at all. Plus, she was snarky.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1533066169i/26057333._SY540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>In this story, she has to go to a ball disguised as her step-sister with her sister's f</span>
  <span id="freeText1818932633361469194" style="display:none">A Cinderella re-telling in Historical Romance? Count me in!<br><br>Except, well, Cinderella was always too much of a victim for me. So, when I met the heroine of this book, Kate, color me surprised. She fought with the evil stepmother constantly, and the only reason she would give in to the stepmother's demands was to protect the servants and tenant farmers. So, I liked her. Not doormatty at all. Plus, she was snarky.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1533066169i/26057333._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In this story, she has to go to a ball disguised as her step-sister with her sister's fiance to get his uncle, the prince's, approval for the marriage. The prince lives in a castle and has a bunch of crazy relatives he is trying to support. Castle-living be expensive, yo. So, he is also supposed to get married to a Russian princess because she's bringing a big ol' dowry to the table. Hey, a prince gotta eat, right?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1533066169i/26057334.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Don't answer that, Rob!<br><br>Along with meeting the prince, Kate also meets Henry, who is a woman. Her godmother. And, she is awesome! She's giving Kate a lot of good advice on men.<br><br><b>
  <i>"Never marry anyone with fewer brains than yourself, darling. It always ends badly."<br><br>"I'm very fond of unquestioning adoration... One can't have too much of it, from dogs or men."<br><br>"Typical of a man. They always die inconveniently."</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533066169ra/26057332.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I was impressed.<br><br>There are several things that would usually trigger me in this book. Starting with the fact that Kate and the Prince fall too fast and are cheating on his fiance, but since this was a "fairy tale" I am willing to give a lot more leeway. Also, though, I would give a LOT of leeway for a book that is this well-written and witty. The banter in this book is amazing! So funny and smart! Even the side characters are so well-developed that I want their stories.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1533066170i/26057335.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" href="/user/show/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish">UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of feel good historical  love stories</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer116913914" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14679386923286136601"><br/><i>
  <b>This is not your mama’s Cinderella story! </b>
</i> <br/><br/>In <i>A Kiss at Midnight</i> we have a Godmother whose wisdom rivals any magic found in a wand, “rats” I wanted to love and cuddle and who’d be welcome at my house anytime, a stepsister who isn’t so wicked, and a step mother who <i>is</i>, a coach to whisk you away at the stroke of midnight, and a prince who is more than just charming, he’s a wonderful, honorable and a worthy human being – not to mention downright sexy!<br/><br/>This was such a delightful re-telling of the</span>
  <span id="freeText14679386923286136601" style="display:none"><br /><i>
  <b>This is not your mama’s Cinderella story! </b>
</i> <br /><br />In <i>A Kiss at Midnight</i> we have a Godmother whose wisdom rivals any magic found in a wand, “rats” I wanted to love and cuddle and who’d be welcome at my house anytime, a stepsister who isn’t so wicked, and a step mother who <i>is</i>, a coach to whisk you away at the stroke of midnight, and a prince who is more than just charming, he’s a wonderful, honorable and a worthy human being – not to mention downright sexy!<br /><br />This was such a delightful re-telling of the classic Cinderella fairytale, presented in a way that makes one believe that finding your very own Prince Charming could happen to anyone. As might be expected, this story is splendid, enchanting and funny, heartwarming and at times heartbreaking, but one thing your mama’s Cinderella didn’t have was the heat between our hero and heroine, Gabriel, the prince and the Kate Daltry, our very own, in the flesh, Cinderella.<br /><br />I’m not going to spend time going over the plot details, as it’s really not necessary. Most all of us have either read the classic or seen this fairytale love story on the big screen, thanks to Walt Disney, and with the exception of a few minor twists to make this fit into “real life,” there’s no question about which fairytale <i>A Kiss at Midnight</i> is spun from.<br /><br />I want to say, Ms. James, thank you for this lovely story. It had me smiling, sighing, laughing out loud and even crying. This is the first book I’ve read by you, and I’m hooked! I’m thrilled to hear that you’ll be writing more in this series and that Wick, dear Wick, will be getting his own story in a novella. Thank you!<br /><br />Dear readers of my review, I urge you, if you’re in the mood for a light, feel good read, pick up this book and allow yourself to be swept away into this grown up Cinderella world, where insignificant little house maids can find their Prince Charming and together live their <i>happily ever after.</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14679386923286136601" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of historical, regency, Cinderella, &amp; fairy tale romances</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=historical-romance-regency">historical-romance-regency</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=favorite-hottest-love-scenes-nookie">favorite-hottest-love-scenes-nookie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=author-eloisa-james">author-eloisa-james</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=enemies-to-lovers-opposites-attract">enemies-to-lovers-opposites-attract</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=hh-aristocracy-nobility-royalty">hh-aristocracy-nobility-royalty</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82771817" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4952179806304424803">3 ½ stars – Historical/Fairy Tale Romance<br/><br/>I had a hard time getting into this book and the first 200 or so pages really dragged for me. To be fair, my lack of enthusiasm was, at least partly, because I probably just wasn’t in the right mood or frame of mind for it. My frustration for about a third of the story was that there were too many characters and just way too much going on, so things were a bit muddled. The main H/H, Kate and Gabriel, seemed to get a bit lost in the chaos and there wasn’t </span>
  <span id="freeText4952179806304424803" style="display:none">3 ½ stars – Historical/Fairy Tale Romance<br /><br />I had a hard time getting into this book and the first 200 or so pages really dragged for me. To be fair, my lack of enthusiasm was, at least partly, because I probably just wasn’t in the right mood or frame of mind for it. My frustration for about a third of the story was that there were too many characters and just way too much going on, so things were a bit muddled. The main H/H, Kate and Gabriel, seemed to get a bit lost in the chaos and there wasn’t nearly enough interaction between them, so it didn’t even feel much like a romance for a significant portion of the story. So up until around page 202, it was really looking like this would be a 2 star read. <br /><br />But then, to my pleasant surprise, once the flirtation and romance between Kate and Gabriel picked up momentum and their characters finally sparked to life, my interest peaked. Their love scenes were achingly tender, utterly romantic, and lushly sensual. Although it took a while for Kate and Gabriel to become a believable romantic couple, once that happened, I found myself rooting strongly for their HEA. Thus, the last 150 pages or so, especially the beautiful, steamy love scenes, made reading and sticking with this through the slow and cluttered parts truly worth it and boosted my rating. And the ending and epilogue were sweet icing on the cake. 3 ½ stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4952179806304424803" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17996758925716512949">4.5<br/>My friends Catherine and Uniquelymoi recommended this book to me, and it is official: they can recommend books to me anytime!<br/><br/>I started this really late, like 10 pm late. I just wanted to read a bit before bed. Big mistake. I got so caught up that I didn't stop reading til about 2 am when I finished the book!<br/><br/>I'm not a huge fan of any new takes on classic fairy tales, so this never rated high on my to-read list, but with the reviews my friends had given this book, I bumped it up. I loved it. I </span>
  <span id="freeText17996758925716512949" style="display:none">4.5<br />My friends Catherine and Uniquelymoi recommended this book to me, and it is official: they can recommend books to me anytime!<br /><br />I started this really late, like 10 pm late. I just wanted to read a bit before bed. Big mistake. I got so caught up that I didn't stop reading til about 2 am when I finished the book!<br /><br />I'm not a huge fan of any new takes on classic fairy tales, so this never rated high on my to-read list, but with the reviews my friends had given this book, I bumped it up. I loved it. I absolutely loved it. This Cinder girl was no doormat for her wicked step-mother, and her half-sister was a sweet girl. The prince was sinful, and the godmother wasn't a fairy by any means, but her "magic" was just as potent.<br /><br />Kate's step-mother comes up with a "brilliant" (insert eye roll here) plan to pass Kate off as her sister Victoria at the court of some random prince's castle, since poor darling Victoria has an infected lip and looks dreadful. Victoria and her fiance Algie need this prince's approval to wed, or he won't get his inheritance. So, since Victoria can't go, Kate goes in her place. Mind you, they are half-sisters, so they only look a little bit alike. Victoria is a pampered and buxom 18 yr old debutante, while Kate is a 23 year old, skinny and tall, and well, she's Kate. But she agrees to this because the prince's approval is needed.<br /><br />So off to meet the Prince.<br /><br />Kate wears these awful wigs (I thought of Kiera Knightly in the Duchess with all those intricate and tall wigs) to disguise her hair, and she and the prince just crack me up.<br /><br />One of my favorite things about this book is that Gabriel figured out fairly quickly, and early on, that she wasn't Victoria. I hate misunderstandings that take up the whole book, so luckily that wasn't the case here.<br /><br />But his guess as to who she really was (he figured she was some illegitimate sister/commoner) irritated me that she didn't set him straight right away. But that little tiny thing is the only thing that bothered me at all. So, woot!<br /><br />Our godmother comes in the form of Henry. She is fabulous! She absolutely stole the show. A fantastic character who, while she may not have had a magic wand, she did some fairly miraculous things. She made sure that Kate got her dowry, for one, thing. Offered her a place to live in London for another. And very succinctly had a way of putting busybodies in their place. bravo Henry! But her coup de grace was when Henry helped Kate get ready for the ball. She was the best godmother any girl could have. And Kate was able to go as herself, not her sister, so she didn't have to wear a wig, and her sweet sister let Kate shine, glass slippers and all. It was fabulous.<br /><br />And our prince was in love with Kate from the first time she ignored his charming, princely self. so for him to even consider marrying the Russian princess infuriated me. But he was so wonderfully in love with Kate that I enjoyed for once seeing the hero pine for the heroine. It was sweet, and sultry and so wonderful.<br /><br />Now, onto my favorite scene. I don't think I've ever done this before, but this was great. Our prince planned a night for Kate that she would never forget, and the best part was watching him strip. I say "watching" because it was so sinfully easy to visualize. It's always the alpha male having his woman strip for him, then he shucks his pants and climbs aboard (not that I don't enjoy that!). But here, he had Kate waiting in his chambers while he dressed for dinner, and he stripped in the most delicious way ever. The simple act of taking off his cufflinks became erotic when Gabriel turned his wrist over to Kate. Standing in only his shirtsleeves, with the front tenting up, and Kate not quite sure what to expect was great. But when he dressed in his silk breeches, and couldn't get his erection to go down, because Kate couldn't stop staring at it..well, let's just say I have a healthy imagination, so I had no trouble picturing that.<br /><br />The ending was sweet, and the love story between the two was achingly beautiful. I haven't cried over a book in a while, and several times I had tears dripping down my cheeks. But I also laughed out loud several times with Kate channeling Cesar Milan the dog whisperer for the little "rats." One of whom Henry kept. And the banter back and forth between Kate and Dante, or Gabriel or even Wick, Gabriel's brother. <br /><br />So, thank you to Catherine and Uniquelymoi for this wonderful book, and I blame you both for me only getting 4 hrs of sleep!<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17996758925716512949" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=library-loan">library-loan</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1193678274" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13476255447277926706">I love fairytale re-tellings and even with this book taking liberties, it was very good and beautifully written. This is my second book by EJ, and I like her style. She hasn't reached the pinnacle of genius like writers Lisa Kleypas and Sherry Thomas in HR, but I enjoy her stuff and may very well need to read more of her work.<br/>Gabriel was quite the sensual man, his characterization was so sexy, with his dark, long hair and sexy seductive accent. I adored his responsibility to his family in the mi</span>
  <span id="freeText13476255447277926706" style="display:none">I love fairytale re-tellings and even with this book taking liberties, it was very good and beautifully written. This is my second book by EJ, and I like her style. She hasn't reached the pinnacle of genius like writers Lisa Kleypas and Sherry Thomas in HR, but I enjoy her stuff and may very well need to read more of her work.<br />Gabriel was quite the sensual man, his characterization was so sexy, with his dark, long hair and sexy seductive accent. I adored his responsibility to his family in the midst of trying to live his own dreams. As a prince, he was more limited in doing what he wanted but he definitely knew WHO he wanted. And it wasn't his chosen princess from Russia, Tatiana. Kate Daltry captured his affections early on and watching him slowly realize she was the ONLY woman for him was sweet. I loved Kate, a great heroine who was quite similar to Gabriel in familial obligations. Together they were electric and the last third was very difficult to put down. This of course ended on a very sweet and fantastical note. The short letter Gabriel sent to Kate towards the end was disarming. He only wrote two sentences but the sheer power behind them was incredible. The epilogue wasn't even needed but was a cute insertion.<br /><br />I heard the rest of the series is great and I'm looking forward to continuing, especially with the re-telling of Beauty And The Beast theme. Anyways, a great story with a lovely cast, I really liked it.</span>

<div id="review_2133677939" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2133677939" />
    <a title="Katherine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13311251-katherine"><img alt="Katherine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577842427p2/13311251.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2133677939?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katherine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katherine" href="/user/show/13311251-katherine">Katherine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=and-we-ll-never-be-royals">and-we-ll-never-be-royals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=instalove-express">instalove-express</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=dem-families-be-cray-cray">dem-families-be-cray-cray</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=dishonor-on-your-cow">dishonor-on-your-cow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=fairytale-retelling">fairytale-retelling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=jolly-old-england">jolly-old-england</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2133677939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5353205256223348348"><b>
  <i>"'Let me sum it up for you: Kate, very sensibly, shows no interest in you. Frightened by the imminent arrival of your bride, you are now running shrieking in the other direction of the one woman who not only doesn't want you, but isn't eligible. Really, could you be a bit more original?'"</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>Synopsis:</b> Cinderella must pretend to be Drusilla for a week so that Drusilla can be approved to marry a puff pastry named Algie, all while being seduced by the one man who needs to approve the union, Prince </span>
  <span id="freeText5353205256223348348" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"'Let me sum it up for you: Kate, very sensibly, shows no interest in you. Frightened by the imminent arrival of your bride, you are now running shrieking in the other direction of the one woman who not only doesn't want you, but isn't eligible. Really, could you be a bit more original?'"</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>Synopsis:</b> Cinderella must pretend to be Drusilla for a week so that Drusilla can be approved to marry a puff pastry named Algie, all while being seduced by the one man who needs to approve the union, Prince Charming. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Biblio-Babble</u>
</b><br /><b>Dream and Your Wish Might Be Bad:</b> First of all, despite what the author would like you to think (including a rather desperate pleading for you to think so in a historical footnote), this is SOOOO not a Cinderella retelling. This is just another historical romp through the Regency era, albeit a bad one. The bare bones plot of Cinderella is there, but everybody else is horrible. Prince Charming is a cad, Cinderella is annoying, the Stepmother acts like she ascended from the 13th Realm of hellfire and damnation, and Victoria (the stepsister) is decidedly not evil. If <i>Before Midnight</i> by Cameron Dokey and this book met, they would have a lot in common. In the sense that though they claim to be Cinderella retellings, they aren’t really ones at all.<br /><br /><b>North South West:</b> I’m not quite sure if author was really serious when it came to naming her characters, or whether it was supposed to be all one big joke. But what can’t be denied is the absolute ridiculousness of the names in this book.<br /><br />Biggitstaff. Mr. Cherryderry. Algerernon, nicknamed Algie by Victoria (you nicknamed him after a type of fungus, really?!!) And best of all….<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Gabriel Albrecht-Frederick William von Aschenberg of Warl-Marburg Baalsfeld.</i>
</b><br /><br />Yes, that’s his real, God-given name. And I thought North West was bad. This is absolutely ridiculous. Not only that, can you imagine what a pain in ass it must have been for the servants to try and fetch the dude when he was a kid. It must’ve taken them at least five minutes for them to get the damn name out, and then they probably would’ve passed out from oxygen deprivation. <br /><br /><b>To Cad or Not to Cad?:</b> Said prince with the long name (I’m just calling him Gabe, because my fingers would murder me if I tried to type out that name every single time), couldn’t really make up his mind whether or not he wanted to be a dick. On the one hand, he could be extremely irritating and wouldn’t take no for an answer (both literally and figuratively). On the other hand, the author decided to make him an Indiana Jones type intellectual who loves archaeology and would rather be in the dust and bones of the desert digging up pottery rather than being a prince. I never did find him appealing as a romantic hero, particularly towards the end, but I guess that was just part of his complicated character.<br /><br /><b>Relationship Status? It’s Complicated:</b> Gabriel and Kate really couldn’t decide what their relationship status was. It sort of played out like this:<br /><br /><b>Kate:</b><i> Please don’t kiss me!</i><br /><b>Gabe:</b> I’m gonna do it anyways.<br /><b>Kate:</b><i> Nevermind, please do kiss me. But don’t even think about taking my virginity.</i><br /><b>Gabe:</b><i> :Yanks off his shirt to showcase his washboard abs:</i><br /><b>Kate:</b><i> What was I saying?<br /><br />:Rips off her dress:</i><br /><br />It was so ducking infuriating. <br /><br /><b>The Case of the Disappearing Prince Charming:</b> So the whole obstacle in Kate and Gabe’s complicated relationship is that Gabe is set to wed a beautiful Russian princess Tatiana. She was actually… nice. There wasn’t anything bad about her. She was rather sweet. She wasn’t catty, she wasn’t bitchy, she was just a nice, normal gal (or as normal as a princess can be). And what does Gabriel do during their coming out ball for their engagement. He locks Kate in his bedroom, runs down to the ball, and then proceeds to run up to his tower two or three times in order to give Kate the best orgasms of her life. All while his fiancé is at the ball.<br /><br />Look, I’m already opposed to cheating. But when the cheating occurs on someone who so obviously doesn’t deserve or warrant is just plain wrong. It tainted my idea of Gabe and Kate as a couple permanently, and coupled with the fact that this was supposed to be a Cinderella retelling made the book just ridiculous. <br /><br /><b>Forget the Slipper, I Want the Godmother:</b> This book probably would’ve only gotten one star if it weren’t for the bright shining character that was Kate’s godmother Henrietta (but please, call her Henry). She’s not a fairy, but what she makes up for in supernatural abilities she makes up for in absolute hilarious dialogue. With the appearance of Cathy Bates and the banter of Whoopi Goldberg, Henry teaches Kate to be a proper lady in society, since Kate is so woefully uneducated. I want Henry just to follow me around and narrate my entire life for me, she’s that good. If there had been more Henry and <br />********************<br />Not even the most talented fairy godmother can save this disaster of a Cinderella retelling due to a caddish hero, an indecisive heroine, and a plot that resembles nothing to Perrault’s fairy tale. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5353205256223348348" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_155632527" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/155632527" />
    <a title="willaful" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2833071-willaful"><img alt="willaful" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1382328800p2/2833071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/155632527?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="willaful" class="user" itemprop="url" name="willaful" href="/user/show/2833071-willaful">willaful</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2833071-willaful?shelf=cant-marry-you">cant-marry-you</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer155632527" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14786469940661548076">What a difficult book to rate... 1/2 bleh + 1/2 awesome = ?<br/><br/>A fairly faithful retelling of “Cinderella,” set in some vaguely Georgian/Regency-ish period, this is the story of Kate, a dispossessed daughter and Gabriel, a prince in need of a wealthy wife. The first half of the book reads like James was channeling Christina Dodd at her weirdest: a scattered, muddled, mishmash of characters, plot and conversations. There’s a bit of sardonic wit, but nothing that made me want to continue; I persisted </span>
  <span id="freeText14786469940661548076" style="display:none">What a difficult book to rate... 1/2 bleh + 1/2 awesome = ?<br /><br />A fairly faithful retelling of “Cinderella,” set in some vaguely Georgian/Regency-ish period, this is the story of Kate, a dispossessed daughter and Gabriel, a prince in need of a wealthy wife. The first half of the book reads like James was channeling Christina Dodd at her weirdest: a scattered, muddled, mishmash of characters, plot and conversations. There’s a bit of sardonic wit, but nothing that made me want to continue; I persisted only because I’d read that it improved. <br /><br />And it did indeed. When Gabriel and Kate begin to seriously interact, the story becomes the most wonderful, tantalizing seduction, with scenes so intimate that you hardly notice that at first they barely touch. There was no annoyance on my part that this couple takes forever to get into bed; I could have read them seducing each other with words for much longer. <br /><br />And my heart broke for them, as they realized, over and over, that they couldn’t possibly be together. The man who has to marry someone else is one of my very favorite historical romance tropes, and I love the suppressed pain we see in the Prince, as he struggles to do what he sees as his duty:<br /><br />“‘I did it,’ Gabriel said, conversationally. ‘I met the woman, the only woman for me. I met her, and now... I’m going to meet my wife.’”<br /><br />It's a shame this wasn't fantastic all the way through, the way <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8449698.When_Beauty_Tamed_the_Beast" title="When Beauty Tamed the Beast by Eloisa James" rel="nofollow noopener">When Beauty Tamed the Beast</a> was. But since the parts that were good were just so, so good, I have to recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14786469940661548076" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_114649393" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/114649393" />
    <a title="Nisha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2451459-nisha"><img alt="Nisha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473558883p2/2451459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/114649393?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nisha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nisha" href="/user/show/2451459-nisha">Nisha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=fantasy-romance">fantasy-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=historicalromance">historicalromance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=rake-player-heroes">rake-player-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=retold-fairy-tales">retold-fairy-tales</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer114649393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7430256563157925156">After hearing raves about this series (specifically <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10219990.When_Beauty_Tamed_the_Beast' title='When Beauty Tamed the Beast by Eloisa James' rel='nofollow noopener'>When Beauty Tamed the Beast</a>), I decided that I should finally read Ms. James' book. I knew going in, it was a take on Cinderella, and I was quite prepared for it. What I was not prepared for was Ms. James' writing. More on that, later.<br/><br/>Kate, our Cinderella, has a dead (philandering when he was alive) father, a vain and slightly evil stepmother, and a newly acknowledged beautiful, but kind half-sister. Through some convoluted situation where said</span>
  <span id="freeText7430256563157925156" style="display:none">After hearing raves about this series (specifically <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10219990.When_Beauty_Tamed_the_Beast" title="When Beauty Tamed the Beast by Eloisa James" rel="nofollow noopener">When Beauty Tamed the Beast</a>), I decided that I should finally read Ms. James' book. I knew going in, it was a take on Cinderella, and I was quite prepared for it. What I was not prepared for was Ms. James' writing. More on that, later.<br /><br />Kate, our Cinderella, has a dead (philandering when he was alive) father, a vain and slightly evil stepmother, and a newly acknowledged beautiful, but kind half-sister. Through some convoluted situation where said half-sister gets bitten by her dog before meeting a prince who has to approve her engagement with her beau, Kate is 'encouraged' to dress up and play her half-sister to save the girl's impending marriage (half-sister is preggers). And so, Kate accompanies the simple minded, Algie (the beau) to the foreign prince's castle. Gabriel appears to be every bit of an arrogant, self-centered prince, who is engaged to marry Princess Tatiana. He develops a fascination toward Kate, first seducing her, then befriending her, and finally loving her. And we discover that the Prince is a much more honorable man than we assumed. To protect his dependents, he chooses to marry money instead of following his heart. Still, he cannot resist the passion between him and Kate, even as he knows that following it would hurt them both.<br /><br />We get a great ensemble of secondary characters, the half-sister, Victoria; her beau, Algie (he became quite adorable); the Prince's all-seeing half-brother, Wick; the elegantly dressed, Toloose; Kate's Godmother, Henry; her husband, Leo (I thought they were a great pair); the dramatic Lady Effie; the three ridiculous yet lovable Maltese, Caesar, Freddie and Coco; the perfect princess bride, Princess Tatiana; and of course, the Prince's elderly relatives (don't remember their names now, but they were fun). All of them were wonderfully entertaining and EJ unwittingly endears us, readers, to them.<br /><br />But, like someone before me said, the first 200 (or more like 150) pages were unfocused and kinda boring (though not unentertaining, does that make any sense?). No real romance or even interaction leading to love takes place. Ms. James' writes in a very entertaining way, that at first seemed almost mean and condescending (maybe that's just me, since this is my first EJ book). But after a while, I could appreciate the wit without being offended. She builds a fantasy world, rather than following the HR vein, and creates a fairy tale, embellishing with quirky, but lovable characters, sensational love scenes, and true emotion. <br /><br />And that's what won me over and forced me to rate this 5 stars. I adored the last third of the book. The romance between Kate and Gabriel came alive and the drama picks up. I loved how no one was a bad guy and that everyone had flaws, even our hero and heroine. Kate succumbs to her passion, despite the consequences (though she enforces the usage of a french letter) and Gabriel chooses duty while hurting his one true love. <br /><br />This was such a gorgeous story and I would recommend it to everyone who loves a fairy tale. Fair warning, this is not a historical romance, even if there was no magic. I just hope that everyone else would enjoy this book as much as I did. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7430256563157925156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_116525453" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/116525453" />
    <a title="KarenH" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2609870-karenh"><img alt="KarenH" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305278962p2/2609870.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/116525453?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="KarenH" class="user" itemprop="url" name="KarenH" href="/user/show/2609870-karenh">KarenH</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2609870-karenh?shelf=keepers">keepers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2609870-karenh?shelf=love-at-first-sight">love-at-first-sight</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2609870-karenh?shelf=audiobooks-that-rock">audiobooks-that-rock</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2609870-karenh?shelf=definitely-worth-your-while">definitely-worth-your-while</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2609870-karenh?shelf=excellent-love-story">excellent-love-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2609870-karenh?shelf=feisty-heroine">feisty-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2609870-karenh?shelf=audiobook-5-stars-plus">audiobook-5-stars-plus</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2609870-karenh?shelf=narrator-extraordinaire">narrator-extraordinaire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2609870-karenh?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer116525453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14195565923189750765">When we were little girls, we all knew the story of Cinderella...the rags to riches to rags plight of an impoverished beauty who is granted one unforgettable night at a glorious ball with a handsome prince. That might have been a long time ago but none of us has forgotten the love story of Cinderella and her Prince Charming...and the most romantic "happily ever after" in fairy-tale land. A Kiss at Midnight is Eloisa James' gift to those little girls - all grown up now but still believing in the </span>
  <span id="freeText14195565923189750765" style="display:none">When we were little girls, we all knew the story of Cinderella...the rags to riches to rags plight of an impoverished beauty who is granted one unforgettable night at a glorious ball with a handsome prince. That might have been a long time ago but none of us has forgotten the love story of Cinderella and her Prince Charming...and the most romantic "happily ever after" in fairy-tale land. A Kiss at Midnight is Eloisa James' gift to those little girls - all grown up now but still believing in the magic of true love, handsome heroes and the perfect, fairy-tale ending.<br><br>This story doesn't have any paranormal tweaks...no rats becoming footmen or pumpkins transformed into carriages. It does, however, have a most charming prince who studies archeology and a palace full of odd animals and even stranger people who the prince has taken under his wing. Alas! What an enormous expense it is to keep them all and so Prince Gabriel is resigned to accepting his arranged betrothal to a wealthy Russian princess.<br><br>Kate Daltry has been living the life of a cast-aside relation for many years. Once her father died, Kate's stepmother completely took over their London estate and set about making Kate's stepsister the belle of the ton. The stepsister, Victoria, manages to snag a peer but due to unfortunate circumstances, cannot accompany said peer to visit his uncle, the prince, to receive a royal blessing on the union. Kate is forced to go in Victoria's place.<br><br>From their first encounter, sparks fly between Kate and Gabriel - and a battle of wits ensues. They are, however, most intrigued by each other; and, managing to spend a great deal of quality time together, are helpless to falling in love. Soon the battle of wits that brought them together transforms, over the course of the story, into a conscientious battle between right and wrong...between letting love rule and loving enough to let go. Add to this dilemma a princess who is not only beautiful but has a sweet countenance as well...also enamored with the prince and by all means has the rights to him...and you've got a twist on the story that no longer resembles the fairy tale. There are many laugh-out-loud moments and a few poignant, tearful scenes made that much worse because there really are no wicked stepmothers to blame for what can never be between Kate and Gabriel. Evil thy name is fate...indestructible and eternal.<br><br>Do not lose sight of your girlhood fantasy, however, as James works a little magic of her own to make things right. And don't be caught up with any historical inadequacies you find (as James points out at the end of the book). Simply take it as it's been presented to you...a grownup version of Cinderella written precisely for the incurable romantic that you undoubtedly are. Perhaps, when you are finished reading the book, you will close your eyes and dream...of beautiful ball gowns, sinfully handsome princes, and the glass slipper you left behind. <br><br>5* stars<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380338364i/695454.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br></span>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth" href="/user/show/1922750-elizabeth">Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer126737534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7180674751750921480">A KISS AT MIDNIGHT is simply enchanting! The heroine is intelligent and strong, the hero is sexy and just a bit dangerous, and the secondary characters are delightfully charming. One of the best books I've read in years!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_108110403" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/108110403" />
    <a title="Catherine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3282244-catherine"><img alt="Catherine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1277923282p2/3282244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/108110403?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catherine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catherine" href="/user/show/3282244-catherine">Catherine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=fairy-tale">fairy-tale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=england">england</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=crazy-family">crazy-family</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer108110403" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6296693154965509969">What a fun book! There's just something special about reading a new twist on a classic story. The romance developed faster than I usually like, but I was expecting that going in. Cinderella doesn't spend months with the prince before falling in love, so how can I expect something different from Kate?<br/><br/>Katherine Daltry, or Kate as she prefers to be called, gets suckered into pretending to be her stepsister, Victoria, for a few days by her stepmother. Kate would be the first person to tell you the d</span>
  <span id="freeText6296693154965509969" style="display:none">What a fun book! There's just something special about reading a new twist on a classic story. The romance developed faster than I usually like, but I was expecting that going in. Cinderella doesn't spend months with the prince before falling in love, so how can I expect something different from Kate?<br /><br />Katherine Daltry, or Kate as she prefers to be called, gets suckered into pretending to be her stepsister, Victoria, for a few days by her stepmother. Kate would be the first person to tell you the deception wouldn't work, but she bargains her cooperation for help for one of the tenants. After Kate's father died her stepmother started letting the estate run ragged and not doing properly by her tenants. <br /><br />Kate doesn't stay with her stepmother and stepsister because she couldn't go somewhere else. She could, she has nothing against going away to be a governess. She just can't stand to abandon her duty to her father's estate. What would happen if she wasn't there to help at least a little? But duty can weigh heavy after a while. Kate is ready for a change.<br /><br />The beginning started rather slowly for me. I found myself bored up until we got to the castle. I wasn't discouraged though. I find that Eloisa James doesn't really shine until there's heavy character interaction and dialogue. When that shows up the book just starts to pop!<br /><br />I was amused by Gabriel and Kate's interaction. They had so much humor and fun in their conversations. I loved all their flirting! Gabriel was the romantic and Kate was the realist. I thought it was hilarious when Gabriel quoted one of Romeo's lines to Kate and she ruins the moment by asking if he kills himself right after that. <br /><br />The author kept a lot of the original story elements. There were glass slippers and a midnight ball and even some rats running around. Although the rats aren't <i>literally</i> rats, thank goodness! There's even a godmother, who has to be my favorite character in the whole book. <br /><br />The godmother, Henry, has a sad past, but she doesn't let it rule her life and she's the best adviser that Kate could ever ask for. She's open to whatever her niece decides, and even encourages her to embrace her naughty side once in a while. I loved watching her interact with her husband. They seem like they have a great relationship, even if he does have a problem or two. I loved how honest Henry was about everything and how she was there for Kate no matter what. I loved the talk she gave Kate about giving Gabriel one more chance to man up and then what to do if he didn't. I've wanted to give that speech to so many romance heroines!<br /><br />If you're bothered by historical inaccuracies, let me help you out. The author discusses her free and loose use of period language in the Historical Note at the end of the book. I wasn't bothered by it, but you might be.<br /><br />This wasn't my favorite book by this author, but I still enjoyed it. I felt the relationship was underdeveloped, but what was there was a lot of fun. The ending was a bit too cutesy for me, but I don't blame the author for wanting to go out with a very sweet HEA for her fairytale. <br /><br />P.S. The "bosom friends" were hilarious. I need to google to see if they really did that!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6296693154965509969" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_176650222" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/176650222" />
    <a title="Duchess Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2204947-duchess-nicole"><img alt="Duchess Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499265843p2/2204947.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/176650222?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Duchess Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Duchess Nicole" href="/user/show/2204947-duchess-nicole">Duchess Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=genre-historical-romance">genre-historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=favorite-heroes">favorite-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=e-pcs">e-pcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer176650222" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14333245688710572233">What a beautiful story! Eloisa James does a lovely job of staying true to the whimsical, ultra romantic aspect of a fairy tale in this retelling of Cinderella. And boy, was it romantic! <br/><br/>Kate is the orphaned girl, with the evil stepmother who basically strips her wealth and status from her after her father's death and passes it on to her own daughter. I like how this element of the story was portrayed. The step-family isn't really evil, they're simply selfish. The step mother isn't even a big par</span>
  <span id="freeText14333245688710572233" style="display:none">What a beautiful story! Eloisa James does a lovely job of staying true to the whimsical, ultra romantic aspect of a fairy tale in this retelling of Cinderella. And boy, was it romantic! <br /><br />Kate is the orphaned girl, with the evil stepmother who basically strips her wealth and status from her after her father's death and passes it on to her own daughter. I like how this element of the story was portrayed. The step-family isn't really evil, they're simply selfish. The step mother isn't even a big part of the story. And the step sister is basically oblivious. So it takes away the villain aspect and lets you focus on the romance.<br /><br />Kate is such a wonderful woman. She's accepted her lot in life, though she knows that she deserves better. But she's found a satisfaction and contentment that is admirable. She doesn't think much of her looks, as they are vastly different from what is considered beautiful. She's been worked skinny, with tan skin and callused hands. Of course, she doesn't see herself as everyone else does.<br /><br />But one thing leads to another, and she is sent to pose as her sister at the home of a foreign prince. Here we meet Prince Gabriel, a man whose responsibilities weigh heavily on his honorable shoulders. He, of course, is drawn to the brown skinned, scrawny woman. He cannot fathom why, but he finds himself seeking her out. She unwittingly brings out his mischievous, playful side. And she doesn't fawn over him, which at first annoys him. Then he realizes that he is allowed to be himself, and that he is falling for this honest, beautiful, mysterious woman claiming to be someone she is not. Yet his duty to his family and country inhibits their relationship, until time runs out. Gabriel must make a final decision, possibly the most important one of his life.<br /><br />By the time I got to the part with the inevitable glass slipper, I was madly in love with this book. It's absolutely, lusciously romantic. Just the kisses are erotic.<br /><br />"...I can't imagine why you're here with me, but I know that you should be in your castle with your guests."<br />"For some reason, I'm mad about your kisses, Kate."<br />Oooooh, shivers! Here's one more:<br /><br />"Do tell," Gabriel said. "Were they kissing the way we do?"<br />He had pulled off his cravat, and his shirt revealed a triangle of chest. It was vastly improper. Kate pulled her gaze away. "We don't kiss in any particular way," she corrected him. "We may have exchanged a few kisses in the past, but-"<br />"We kiss as if the bloody room had burst on fire," he interrupted. "We kiss as if making love didn't exist and kissing was all there was." <br /><br />Gotta love a man who knows how to kiss! And...other things. Wonderful story, told by one of my favorite historical romance authors. And this book proves why. I am so glad that this is the first of a series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14333245688710572233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_119328875" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119328875" />
    <a title=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida"><img alt=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1295034921p2/1453659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119328875?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" href="/user/show/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida"> Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to  Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~* by: </span>
      Dhestiny's and Rane's Reviews ...and Quinn's enticing quotes.
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida?shelf=owned-read">owned-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida?shelf=romance-historical">romance-historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida?shelf=owned-unread">owned-unread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida?shelf=fairytale-retells">fairytale-retells</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119328875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6866552473428129929"><b>2.5-3 of 5 Stars</b> - <b>
  <i>Also reviewed at: <a href='http://ladyjaynesreadingden.blogspot.com/2011/12/2.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lady Jayne's Reading Den</a></i>
</b> <br/><br/><b>Did Not Finish<br/><br/>*WARNING: This review contains a SPOILER of a particular scene in the book which I had an issue with.* </b> <br/><br/>This is a Cinderella re-telling.<br/><br/>I still haven’t finished this, after putting it aside for several months, and I’ve finally accepted that I don’t think I feel like finishing it. *sad sigh* :-(<br/><br/>I'm sorry, friends, I have tried to pick it back up a few times but just can't seem to keep reading.<br/><br/>I don’t know what happene</span>
  <span id="freeText6866552473428129929" style="display:none"><b>2.5-3 of 5 Stars</b> - <b>
  <i>Also reviewed at: <a href="http://ladyjaynesreadingden.blogspot.com/2011/12/2.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Lady Jayne's Reading Den</a></i>
</b> <br /><br /><b>Did Not Finish<br /><br />*WARNING: This review contains a SPOILER of a particular scene in the book which I had an issue with.* </b> <br /><br />This is a Cinderella re-telling.<br /><br />I still haven’t finished this, after putting it aside for several months, and I’ve finally accepted that I don’t think I feel like finishing it. *sad sigh* :-(<br /><br />I'm sorry, friends, I have tried to pick it back up a few times but just can't seem to keep reading.<br /><br />I don’t know what happened. I think I just didn’t <i>CONNECT</i> with the characters in this book. I know a lot of my Goodreads friends really enjoyed this, though, and I’m going against the grain here… and not to detract from others’ love of the book… but I struggled with it.<br /><br />If you see my status, you’d probably say, you’ve come so close, why not finish it? <br /><br />It was enjoyable enough to start off with - was pretty cute, in fact, but at the same time, was all too easy for me to put down and felt slow. And then… Well…I didn’t like that the prince was going to seduce, and had the heroine waiting in his room, while he had to go and entertain his betrothed princess at the ball. It made me incredibly uncomfortable. <br /><br />I have forgiven cheating in books, before, because I had truly connected with the characters, felt really strongly for them, and was able to forgive them a grave mistake. But with this? I really don’t know……I just <i>really</i> didn’t like the thought of the prince actually having the woman he had fallen for waiting for him, in his bath, while he went off to meet and dance with another woman; the woman he was going to marry, out of duty. It did not sit right with me. I just didn't feel it fair to any of them. And I hadn’t really realised, at the time that I set it aside, how much this actually bothered me. But now when I think of this book, it's all I can think about, so I find that just can’t bring myself to continue reading to get to the actual love scene between Prince Gabriel and Kate. <br /><br />This is MY issue and I feel bad for giving up on this book, but with all the books out there I want to read – there are SO MANY! - I just can’t bring myself to continue. <br /><br />I also feel bad for giving it 2.5-3 Stars, but my rating is based not wholly on an assessment of the author’s writing abilities, but rather on my own level of enjoyment of the book. <br /><br />I’m sorry, Eloisa James. I <i>will</i> give your other books a go, though. <br /><br />If you are a reader who hasn’t read this book, as I said, many loved/liked it, so you may, too. <br /><br />I did, however, love these quotes (below) that Quinn had shared in her Goodreads status updates and which enticed me to read this. There were some tingly moments between the hero and heroine, but just not enough interaction between them, for my liking, for me to connect with them and care about seeing their Happily-Ever-After.<blockquote><i>‘"Do tell," Gabriel said. "Were they kissing the way we do?" <br /><br />He had pulled off his cravat, and his shirt revealed a triangle of chest. It was vastly improper. Kate pulled her gaze away. "</i>We<i> don't kiss in any particular way," she corrected him. "We may have exchanged a few kisses in the past, but --" <br /><br />"We kiss as if the bloody room had burst on fire," he interrupted. "We kiss as if making love didn't exist and kissing was all there was.”’<br />…<br />‘He took the word from her lips. Their kiss was as untamed as the garden they stood in. It was the kind of kiss that skirted the edge of propriety even though his hands stayed at her back, and hers around his neck.<br /><br />It skirted propriety because they both knew the kiss was like making love, that there was an exchange, a possession and a submission, a giving and a taking, a forbidden intimacy.’</i></blockquote><br />Great quotes.<br /><br />P.S. The “bosom friends” were funny. ^_^<br /><br />P.P.S. Maybe one day I’ll go back and finish this, and maybe I’ll feel differently about it.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6866552473428129929" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer8339333587177114500"><b>First half - 1 star<br/>Second half - 5 stars</b><br/><br/>Seeing as it's a historical retelling of Cinderella, I was pretty excited about reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6957682.A_Kiss_at_Midnight__Fairy_Tales___1_' title='A Kiss at Midnight (Fairy Tales, #1) by Eloisa James' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Kiss at Midnight</a>. It'd been a while since I'd read a good forbidden romance themed novel, but the beginning was dull enough that I was certain this one wasn't going to change that. Thankfully, the story became absolutely magical during the last hundred pages and saved this from being a complete disappointment. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6957682.A_Kiss_at_Midnight__Fairy_Tales___1_' title='A Kiss at Midnight (Fairy Tales, #1) by Eloisa James' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Kiss at Midnight</a> is my first read by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/86778.Eloisa_James' title='Eloisa James' rel='nofollow noopener'>Eloisa James</a> and I'</span>
  <span id="freeText8339333587177114500" style="display:none"><b>First half - 1 star<br>Second half - 5 stars</b><br><br>Seeing as it's a historical retelling of Cinderella, I was pretty excited about reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6957682.A_Kiss_at_Midnight__Fairy_Tales___1_" title="A Kiss at Midnight (Fairy Tales, #1) by Eloisa James" rel="nofollow noopener">A Kiss at Midnight</a>. It'd been a while since I'd read a good forbidden romance themed novel, but the beginning was dull enough that I was certain this one wasn't going to change that. Thankfully, the story became absolutely magical during the last hundred pages and saved this from being a complete disappointment. <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6957682.A_Kiss_at_Midnight__Fairy_Tales___1_" title="A Kiss at Midnight (Fairy Tales, #1) by Eloisa James" rel="nofollow noopener">A Kiss at Midnight</a> is my first read by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/86778.Eloisa_James" title="Eloisa James" rel="nofollow noopener">Eloisa James</a> and I'm disappointed to say that the writing was altogether lackluster and the story wasn't as interesting as it could have <i>easily</i> been. In addition, the chapters' endings were extremely abrupt and I found myself re-reading them several times before convincing myself that I hadn't missed anything important. This made me feel rather disconcerted throughout the book.<br><br>Gabriel was absolutely wonderful, but Kate's personality didn't impress me at all. The side characters, however, were well-rounded and lovable (especially Henry and Wick) and made the story much more lively than it would've been otherwise.<br><br> The ending was fantastic and everything I'd initially expected from the novel. Unfortunately, it took such a long time to get there that it did little to change my overall impression. <br><br>To sum it up, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6957682.A_Kiss_at_Midnight__Fairy_Tales___1_" title="A Kiss at Midnight (Fairy Tales, #1) by Eloisa James" rel="nofollow noopener">A Kiss at Midnight</a> was a boring and entirely forgettable story, which could have been a lot better if not for the slow beginning and Kate's dull personality. The next book (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8449698.When_Beauty_Tamed_the_Beast__Fairy_Tales___2_" title="When Beauty Tamed the Beast (Fairy Tales, #2) by Eloisa James" rel="nofollow noopener">When Beauty Tamed the Beast</a>) is a retelling of my favorite fairy tale though, so I'm pretty sure I'll be continuing with the series. <br><br><b>For more reviews, visit my blog:<br> <a href="http://zombiehazard.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340428i/696822.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a></b></span>
