<div id="review_146649028" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/146649028" />
    <a title="Quinn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2310262-quinn"><img alt="Quinn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300839213p2/2310262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/146649028?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Quinn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Quinn" href="/user/show/2310262-quinn">Quinn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2310262-quinn?shelf=library-book">library-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2310262-quinn?shelf=regency-victorian-georgian">regency-victorian-georgian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer146649028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14868198153965259763">In the author’s note in the back of this book, Eloisa James writes “<i>A Kiss at Midnight</i>, I cannot emphasize too firmly, is a fairy tale, not an historical novel.” I think this statement would have benefited from being at the front of the book. Whether that would have improved my enjoyment of the first part of this novel is unlikely, but I think I would have preferred that knowledge going in.<br/><br/>For the first several chapters of this novel (in fact, it was probably more like a third of the book), I wa</span>
  <span id="freeText14868198153965259763" style="display:none">In the author’s note in the back of this book, Eloisa James writes “<i>A Kiss at Midnight</i>, I cannot emphasize too firmly, is a fairy tale, not an historical novel.” I think this statement would have benefited from being at the front of the book. Whether that would have improved my enjoyment of the first part of this novel is unlikely, but I think I would have preferred that knowledge going in.<br /><br />For the first several chapters of this novel (in fact, it was probably more like a third of the book), I was scratching my head wondering how it could have possibly garnered so many glowing reviews. It did not capture my interest, was clunky to read and seemed to be lacking direction and style. Worse, Gabriel, the hero and ‘Prince Charming’ was not an appealing or particularly likeable character for more than half the book.<br /><br />But when things picked up, they really picked up. There was delightful dialogue, an eclectic cast of secondary characters (including three wonderfully rendered dogs), and some of the most lusciously described kisses I have had the pleasure of reading, leading to a truly memorable and undeniably sexy episode (which in itself was worth the price of admission). Thankfully, this is a fairytale for adults.<br /><br />There is probably no need to rehash the plot – who doesn’t know the story of Cinderella? The author’s inspiration is obvious, and many elements of the original fairytale have been used in this rendition – glass slippers, wicked stepmothers, godmothers (although not of the fairy persuasion) and hidden identity to name a few, but the author has also very much made this story her own.<br /><br />The intrusions and complications of ‘real life’ mark Eloisa James’ story, and the happy-ever-after is not easily or magically obtained. Our prince is not free to marry as he chooses due to his pressing and significant financial concerns. There is no possible way he could even consider our impoverished and possibly illegitimate heroine as his potential princess, despite his fascination for her.<br /><br />I started out not particularly liking either of our lead characters, but I warmed to Kate fairly quickly, with her frank and outspoken nature, her wit and intelligence. Gabriel took a little longer to warm to, but when I did, he made sure it was worth the wait. Their scenes together were wonderful.<br /><br />If you have yet to read this novel and decide to give it a try, make sure you persist past the halfway mark, because a treasure awaits. This was my first Eloisa James novel, and I will definitely be reading more of her <i>Happily Ever Afters</i> series, with the hope that they wont start out as rough as this one, because when she’s good, she’s really, really good.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14868198153965259763" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manda Collins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manda Collins" href="/user/show/901036-manda-collins">Manda Collins</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/901036-manda-collins?shelf=regency-historical">regency-historical</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer73918678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18199199672830688012">Fabulous retelling of Cinderella with all the wit and charm one would expect from Eloisa James. I loved the little tweaks she gave to the traditional fairy tale elements--an earthy godmother, a not so ugly stepsister, and a not-quite-glass slipper. And of course there was more to the relationship between Kate and her handsome prince than just one evening together at the ball. From their prickly first meeting to their growing attraction to one another, their chemistry zings off the page. James do</span>
  <span id="freeText18199199672830688012" style="display:none">Fabulous retelling of Cinderella with all the wit and charm one would expect from Eloisa James. I loved the little tweaks she gave to the traditional fairy tale elements--an earthy godmother, a not so ugly stepsister, and a not-quite-glass slipper. And of course there was more to the relationship between Kate and her handsome prince than just one evening together at the ball. From their prickly first meeting to their growing attraction to one another, their chemistry zings off the page. James does a fabulous job of building their appreciation for one another and that combined with their wanting makes their HEA not only expected, but inevitable. These two belong together, and unlike the all too brief original fairy tale, James tells us, beautifully, why. This is going straight to my keeper shelf. (As soon as I buy my own copy--this one I read was an ARC loaned to me by a friend who, oddly enough, wants it back;) Loved. This. Book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18199199672830688012" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText2215974700057174418" style="display:none">This was an absolute delight to read. We have you down-trodden beautiful maiden, a gorgeous dark prince, an evil step-mother and a sweet step-sister. Oh yes and a fairy god-mother named Henry....all the makings for a sweet fairy tale and of course this was...with the required happy ending. Kate's step-mother insists that she go to a ball in her step-sister's place due to the actions of a dog. She goes to the ball and of course meets the handsome prince. <br /><br />He is a sweet and caring prince at heart and must therefore do his duty. Kate is no young miss and takes no guff off the prince nor lets him get too big for his britches. The entire story was refreshing and I finished reading it with a smile on my face. Bravo Ms. James. :-) </span>

<div id="review_201922524" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/201922524" />
    <a title="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship"><img alt="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1297107033p2/2109885.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/201922524?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" href="/user/show/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship">Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8680663-a-kiss-at-midnight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=british">british</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=1st-in-series">1st-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer201922524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5574144382632467486">I'm fairly new to historical romance but this was very disappointing fare from what I perceive to be a popular author of the genre. <br/><br/>Though funny at times, I found this book to be insubstantial and inconsistent fluff with a couple I didn't think were "made for each other" at all. The Prince wasn't drawn in a very favourable light (you get the feeling he's a useless arrogant rake) until we're told he has a degree from Oxford in archaeology and the weight of responsibility on his shoulders which me</span>
  <span id="freeText5574144382632467486" style="display:none">I'm fairly new to historical romance but this was very disappointing fare from what I perceive to be a popular author of the genre. <br /><br />Though funny at times, I found this book to be insubstantial and inconsistent fluff with a couple I didn't think were "made for each other" at all. The Prince wasn't drawn in a very favourable light (you get the feeling he's a useless arrogant rake) until we're told he has a degree from Oxford in archaeology and the weight of responsibility on his shoulders which meant he needed to marry an heiress in order to keep his castle full of outcast (and charming) relatives running, thereby giving him the air of an honourable gentleman. I didn't quite buy it. And to a certain extent, neither did Kate.<br /><br />24-year-old "I'm over-the-hill" Kate as our downtrodden Cinderella also isn't the most endearing. Despite being intelligent and witty she's always moaning about her looks (she's not ugly, just under-nourished), her stupid "bosom friends" (wax inserts to enhance ones chest i.e. the ye olde version of chicken fillets) and pining for a man she can't have. <br /><br />Their scenes together weren't all bad, witty banter aside I merely felt their relationship would be more of a fling. Berwick appeared to be a better fit or even the slightly boring Lord Hathaway who seemed charmed by her personality.<br /><br />The ending left me cold. Kate is the one with all the power to grant both herself and her Prince happiness but she fails to do anything, instead leaving him to agonise over a choice: feed his family by marrying the Russian heiress or marry the seemingly penniless Kate and starve. The way she sat back and waited for him to choose her was cruel to both of them. She knew if he wasn't so desperate for money he'd marry her in a heartbeat so he couldn't be compared to her father who was marrying her mother more for greed than necessity when he rejected Henry. Not only that but if she cared for the tenants of her father's estate so much then why didn't she immediately purchase it from her stepmother upon receiving her inheritance? <br /><br />Despite being a "retelling" it bore very little resemblance to the fairy tale, and I don't just mean the Disney version. The stepmother though manipulative, controlled very little. She allowed her daughter and step-daughter to walk around without supervision i.e. governesses and chaperones, which sees her daughter falling pregnant out of wedlock because she failed to educate her on sex.<br /><br />Kate's godmother Henry, although I liked her I was uncomfortable with her connection to Kate's father. It seemed inappropriate that he would ask her to be Kate's godmother so I understood why Henry never took the responsibility seriously until now.<br /><br />This wasn't exactly compelling reading however, the side characters were far more interesting than the leads: Henry and her husband Leo, Berwick and Effie (I loved how the Prince defended her honour and dealt with Beckham) even the horrible yapping dogs (three tiny Malteses -ew!), the lion, elephant and monkey were entertaining. <br /><br />Although the author states this was 'not an historical novel' but a fairy tale she does estimate it was set around 1813 though I had my doubts. Powdered wigs were out of fashion at that time -they went out with the fall of Marie Antoinette (1793). I only mention this because their abundant use, especially the ridiculous rainbow-coloured wigs Kate wore, annoyed the hell out of me. <br /><br />I'll most likely give the author a second chance with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8449698.When_Beauty_Tamed_the_Beast__Happily_Ever_Afters___2_" title="When Beauty Tamed the Beast (Happily Ever Afters, #2) by Eloisa James" rel="nofollow noopener">When Beauty Tamed the Beast</a> but only because the ratings are quite a bit better than this one.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Favourite Quotes</u>
</b><br />"Why did Ceasar bite Victoria, anyway? I never thought to ask."<br />"She was feeding him from her mouth."<br />"<i>What?</i>"<br /><br />"He's male. I've noticed that sometimes the brains simply get left out of the package." ~ Kate<br /><br />"I've no dogs, but I'm willing to consider the lion as a substitute." ~ Prince (Gabriel)<br /><br />"As long as you're not as much a fool as your sister, there's no need to fuss about a bit of liberty before marriage. Just squeak loudly on your wedding night and your husband will never know." ~Henry<br /><br />"Are your footmen unfortunate degenerates?" Henry put in cheerfully. "The only one of those in my household is my darling Leo."<br />They all glanced at Henry's husband, seated opposite her. Leo gave Kate a naughty wink and said, "It takes a degenerate to keep track of my wife, I assure you. No one else would have the imagination."<br /><br />"If my wife had gone to Oxford, they would have had to create a triple first," Leo said.<br />"What did you say?" Henry asked.<br />"In seduction," he whispered.<br /><br />"Offer me a post as your mistress and I'll stab you with a fork, just as Effie stabbed Beckham. Except the fork won't go in your hand." ~Kate<br /><br />"Dear me," Gabriel commented. "England seems to have suffered a rash of trollopy young ladies without fathers." </span>
  <a data-text-id="5574144382632467486" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_934746447" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/934746447" />
    <a title="Paige  Bookdragon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15550986-paige-bookdragon"><img alt="Paige  Bookdragon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570121828p2/15550986.jpg" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer6130399649694375244"><br/>Thought: <i> I didn't know this book was a <b> reread </b> until the lion was mentioned. Ooops.</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427725127i/14312771._SY540_.jpg' width='454' height='548' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>Did you know?<br/><br/>I'm in love with the secondary character. I started looking forward to read about <b> Berwick </b>, the hero's illigetimate brother who works as the majordomo to his castle. He's just sooo cute and he absolutely has a great sense of--(background noise) <i> What? I didn't hear you..This should be a review between Gabriel and Kate?... But I love Wick!....Hmm.Hmmm....B-but this is my review.I gotta to---Ugh. Fin</i></span>
  <span id="freeText6130399649694375244" style="display:none"><br>Thought: <i> I didn't know this book was a <b> reread </b> until the lion was mentioned. Ooops.</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427725127i/14312771._SY540_.jpg" width="454" height="548" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Did you know?<br><br>I'm in love with the secondary character. I started looking forward to read about <b> Berwick </b>, the hero's illigetimate brother who works as the majordomo to his castle. He's just sooo cute and he absolutely has a great sense of--(background noise) <i> What? I didn't hear you..This should be a review between Gabriel and Kate?... But I love Wick!....Hmm.Hmmm....B-but this is my review.I gotta to---Ugh. Fine.. </i><br><br>Let me start again.<br><br>This is the second historical romance with a fairytale retelling twist that I've read. The first one was Julia Quinn's An offer from a gentleman, and although my heart belongs to Benedict, I have to admit that Gabriel is a lovable hero. He's a funny prince who acts accordingly to the time period and he's dashing in a way that if you met this type of person in real life, either you'll melt at his feet or invite him into a drink and be best buddies.<br><br><br>Weird, I know.<br><br>Let's talk about Kate. She's a rare heroine for this type of genre and she's been added to my heroine who doesn't annoy me list. <br><br>Here's the reason why I like her.<br><br>•She's not afraid to speak up her mind and be a pest to her stepmother.<br><br>• She's funny.<br><br>• She's not annoying. Or she didn't do anything that annoys me.<br><br>•She's not the typical regency heroine who whimpers and faints.<br><br><br>And that's it. I have to read Wick's story now because I don't particularly care about the main H/H. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="6130399649694375244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nFk5x7I7OBfvbC/atWPWW6z4THakL3lAEnGXObWTmJUkYsT/vNwsfs5jaisI/S+gml/u/NNZeMzivF7etSI20w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yRjj0WyMF3etO9IvnpIMp3ybNMsC+X0Unt3eD5ZrmHNxIx7pYmsDHow0l94jDPVcSjyWQXWPfJhuEBfolto2NQ==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/86778.Eloisa_James">About Eloisa James</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/86778.Eloisa_James"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1375996000p3/86778.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/86778.Eloisa_James">Eloisa James
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
7,124
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer866411131878678842"><i>New York Times</i> bestselling author Eloisa James writes historical romances for HarperCollins Publishers. Her novels have been published to great acclaim. A reviewer from <i>USA Today</i> wrote of Eloisa's very first book that she "found herself devouring the book like a dieter with a Hershey bar"; later <i>People Magazine</i> raved that "romance writing does not get much better than this." Her novels have repeat</span>
  <span id="freeText866411131878678842" style="display:none"><i>New York Times</i> bestselling author Eloisa James writes historical romances for HarperCollins Publishers. Her novels have been published to great acclaim. A reviewer from <i>USA Today</i> wrote of Eloisa's very first book that she "found herself devouring the book like a dieter with a Hershey bar"; later <i>People Magazine</i> raved that "romance writing does not get much better than this." Her novels have repeatedly received starred reviews from <i>Publishers' Weekly</i> and <i>Library Journal</i> and regularly appear on the best-seller lists.<br /><br />After graduating from Harvard University, Eloisa got an M.Phil. from Oxford University, a Ph.D. from Yale and eventually became a Shakespeare professor, publishing an academic book with Oxford University Press. Currently she is an associate professor and head of the Creative Writing program at Fordham University in New York City. Her "double life" is a source of fascination to the media and her readers. In her professorial guise, she's written a <i>New York Times</i> op-ed defending romance, as well as articles published everywhere from women's magazines such as More to writers' journals such as the <i>Romance Writers' Report</i>.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Eloisa...on her double life:</b>
</i><br /><br />When I'm not writing novels, I'm a Shakespeare professor. It's rather like having two lives. The other day I bought a delicious pink suit to tape a television segment on romance; I'll never wear that suit to teach in, nor even to give a paper at the Shakespeare Association of America conference. It's like being Superman, with power suits for both lives. Yet the literature professor in me certainly plays into my romances. <i>The Taming of the Duke</i> (April 2006) has obvious Shakespearean resonances, as do many of my novels. I often weave early modern poetry into my work; the same novel might contain bits of Catullus, Shakespeare and anonymous bawdy ballads from the 16th century.<br /><br />When I rip off my power suit, whether it's academic or romantic, underneath is the rather tired, chocolate-stained sweatshirt of a mom. Just as I use Shakespeare in my romances, I almost always employ my experiences as a mother. When I wrote about a miscarriage in <i>Midnight Pleasures</i>, I used my own fears of premature birth; when the little girl in <i>Fool For Love</i> threw up and threw up, I described my own daughter, who had that unsavory habit for well over her first year of life.<br /><br />So I'm a writer, a professor, a mother - and a wife. My husband Alessandro is Italian, born in Florence. We spend the lazy summer months with his mother and sister in Italy. It always strikes me as a huge irony that as a romance writer I find myself married to a knight, a <i>cavaliere</i>, as you say in Italian.<br /><br />One more thing...I'm a friend. I have girlfriends who are writers and girlfriends who are Shakespeare professors. And I have girlfriends who are romance readers. In fact, we have something of a community going on my website. Please stop by and join the conversation on my readers' pages.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="866411131878678842" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
